Judges and prosecutors that have made decisions in favor of Correa in his lawsuits have received permanent posts, while others with better assessment grades have been rejected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reformahasta2015_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reformahasta2015-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1936" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG/220px-Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG/330px-Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG/440px-Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sea_lion_sleeping_on_bench_in_Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno_2013.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adult <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_sea_lion" title="Gal&#225;pagos sea lion">Gal&#225;pagos sea lion</a> resting on a park bench in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Baquerizo_Moreno" title="Puerto Baquerizo Moreno">Puerto Baquerizo Moreno</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The laws also forbid articles and media messages that could favor or disfavor some political message or candidate. In the first half of 2012, twenty private TV or radio stations were closed down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw_27-3"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2012 the officials warned the judges that they would be sanctioned and possibly dismissed if they allowed the citizens to appeal to the protection of their constitutional rights against the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw_27-4"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p>People engaging in public protests against environmental and other issues are prosecuted for "terrorism and sabotage", which may lead to an eight-year prison sentence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw_27-5"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_affairs">Foreign affairs</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Ecuador" title="Foreign relations of Ecuador">Foreign relations of Ecuador</a></div>\n<p>Ecuador\'s principal foreign policy objectives have traditionally included defense of its territory from external aggression and support for the objectives of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and the OAS. Ecuador\'s membership in the OPEC in the 1970s and 1980s allowed Ecuadorian leaders to exercise somewhat greater foreign policy autonomy. In Antarctica, Ecuador has maintained a peaceful research station for scientific study as a member nation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antarctica_Treaty" title="Antarctica Treaty">Antarctica Treaty</a>. Ecuador has often placed great emphasis on multilateral approaches to international issues. Ecuador is a member of the United Nations (and most of its specialized agencies) and a member of many regional groups, including the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Group" title="Rio Group">Rio Group</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Economic_System" title="Latin American Economic System">Latin American Economic System</a>, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_American_Energy_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Latin American Energy Organization (page does not exist)">Latin American Energy Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Integration_Association" title="Latin American Integration Association">Latin American Integration Association</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolivarian_Alliance_for_the_Americas" title="Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas">Bolivarian Alliance for the Peoples of Our America</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andean_Community_of_Nations" title="Andean Community of Nations">Andean Community of Nations</a>, the Union of South American Nations (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNASUR" title="UNASUR">UNASUR</a>), and The Bank of the South (Spanish: Banco del Sur or BancoSur).\n</p><p>The Ecuadorian government commits itself to upholding a <a href="/wiki/Progressivism" title="Progressivism">progressive</a> attitude towards <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">migration</a> related problems, <a href="/wiki/Manifesto" title="Manifesto">declaring</a> its <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a> <i>"Ministry of Foreign Affairs and Human Mobility"</i> (Spanish: <i>Ministerio de Relaciones Exteriores y Movilidad Humana</i>). In 2017, the Ecuadorian parliament adopted a <i>Law on human mobility</i> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>. In 2018 the ministry presented a new <i>Human Mobility National Plan</i>, based on policies aimed at promoting universal citizenship and free mobility in the international sphere; generate conditions to promote an orderly and safe migration, strengthen the protection of the rights of this population and defend its diversity, integration, and coexistence. \n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">International Organization for Migration</a> lauds Ecuador as the first state to have established the promotion of the concept of universal citizenship in its <a href="/wiki/2008_Constitution_of_Ecuador" title="2008 Constitution of Ecuador">constitution</a>, aiming to promote the universal recognition and protection of the human rights of migrants. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>]\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Ecuador" title="Provinces of Ecuador">Provinces of Ecuador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Ecuador" title="Cantons of Ecuador">Cantons of Ecuador</a></div>\n<p>Ecuador is divided into 24 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Ecuador" title="Provinces of Ecuador">provinces</a> (Spanish: <i lang="es">provincias</i>), each with its own administrative capital:\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" divided into <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Ecuador" title="Cantons of Ecuador">cantons</a> and further subdivided into parishes (<i>parroquias</i>).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions_and_planning_areas">Regions and planning areas</span></h3>\n<p>Regionalization, or zoning, is the union of two or more adjoining provinces in order to decentralize the administrative functions of the capital Quito.\nIn Ecuador there are seven regions or zones, each shaped by the following provinces:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Region 1 (42,126&#160;km&#178;, or 16,265&#160;mi&#178;): <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esmeraldas_(province)" title="Esmeraldas (province)">Esmeraldas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carchi" title="Carchi">Carchi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imbabura_Province" title="Imbabura Province">Imbabura</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sucumbios" title="Sucumbios">Sucumbios</a>. Administrative city: <a href="/wiki/Ibarra,_Ecuador" title="Ibarra, Ecuador">Ibarra</a></li>\n<li>Region 2 (43,498&#160;km&#178;, or 16,795&#160;mi&#178;): <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pichincha_(province)" title="Pichincha (province)">Pichincha</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napo_(province)" title="Napo (province)">Napo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Orellana_Province" title="Orellana Province">Orellana</a>. Administrative city: <a href="/wiki/Tena,_Ecuador" title="Tena, Ecuador">Tena</a></li>\n<li>Region 3 (44,710&#160;km&#178;, or 17,263&#160;mi&#178;): <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chimborazo_(province)" title="Chimborazo (province)">Chimborazo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tungurahua_(province)" title="Tungurahua (province)">Tungurahua</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pastaza_(province)" title="Pastaza (province)">Pastaza</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cotopaxi_(province)" title="Cotopaxi (province)">Cotopaxi</a>. Administrative city: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riobamba,_Ecuador" title="Riobamba, Ecuador">Riobamba</a></li>\n<li>Region 4 (22,257&#160;km&#178;, or 8,594&#160;mi&#178;): <a href="/wiki/Manab%C3%AD_Province" title="Manab&#237; Province">Manab&#237;</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo_de_los_Tsachilas" title="Santo Domingo de los Tsachilas">Santo Domingo de los Tsachilas</a>. Administrative city: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ciudad_Alfaro,_Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ciudad Alfaro, Ecuador (page does not exist)">Ciudad Alfaro</a></li>\n<li>Region 5 (38,420&#160;km&#178;, or 14,834&#160;mi&#178;): <a href="/wiki/Santa_Elena_Province" title="Santa Elena Province">Santa Elena</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guayas_(province)" title="Guayas (province)">Guayas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_R%C3%ADos_Province" title="Los R&#237;os Province">Los R&#237;os</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos" title="Gal&#225;pagos">Gal&#225;pagos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Province_(Ecuador)" title="Bol&#237;var Province (Ecuador)">Bol&#237;var</a>. Administrative city: <a href="/wiki/Milagro,_Ecuador" title="Milagro, Ecuador">Milagro</a></li>\n<li>Region 6 (38,237&#160;km&#178;, or 14,763&#160;mi&#178;): <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1ar_Province,_Ecuador" title="Ca&#241;ar Province, Ecuador">Ca&#241;ar</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azuay" title="Azuay">Azuay</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morona_Santiago" title="Morona Santiago">Morona Santiago</a>. Administrative city: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuenca_(Ecuador)" title="Cuenca (Ecuador)">Cuenca</a></li>\n<li>Region 7 (27,571&#160;km&#178;, or 10,645&#160;mi&#178;): <a href="/wiki/El_Oro_Province" title="El Oro Province">El Oro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loja_Province" title="Loja Province">Loja</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zamora_Chinchipe" title="Zamora Chinchipe">Zamora Chinchipe</a>. Administrative city: <a href="/wiki/Loja,_Ecuador" title="Loja, Ecuador">Loja</a></li></ul>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a> are Metropolitan Districts. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos" title="Gal&#225;pagos">Gal&#225;pagos</a>, despite being included within Region 5,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> is also under a special unit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Ecuador" title="Military of Ecuador">Military of Ecuador</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Superpuma-ecu.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="316" data-file-width="551" decoding="async" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Superpuma-ecu.JPG/220px-Superpuma-ecu.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Superpuma-ecu.JPG/330px-Superpuma-ecu.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Superpuma-ecu.JPG/440px-Superpuma-ecu.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Superpuma-ecu.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puma_helicopter" title="Puma helicopter">Puma helicopter</a> from the Army\'s Aviation Branch</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kfir_CE_front.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Kfir_CE_front.JPG/220px-Kfir_CE_front.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Kfir_CE_front.JPG/330px-Kfir_CE_front.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Kfir_CE_front.JPG/440px-Kfir_CE_front.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kfir_CE_front.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Air_Force" title="Ecuadorian Air Force">Ecuadorian Air Force</a> (FAE)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Submarino_Shyri.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Submarino_Shyri.jpg/220px-Submarino_Shyri.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Submarino_Shyri.jpg/330px-Submarino_Shyri.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a9/Submarino_Shyri.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Submarino_Shyri.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Shyri_(SS-101)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="BAE Shyri (SS-101) (page does not exist)">BAE Shyri (SS-101)</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;[<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAE_Shyri_(SS-101)" title="es:BAE Shyri (SS-101)">es</a>]</span> from the Ecuadorian Navy.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Ecuador" title="Military of Ecuador">Ecuadorian Armed Forces</a> (Fuerzas Armadas del Ecuador), consists of the <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Army" title="Ecuadorian Army">Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Air_Force" title="Ecuadorian Air Force">Air Force</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Navy" title="Ecuadorian Navy">Navy</a> and have the stated responsibility for the preservation of the integrity and national sovereignty of the national territory.\n</p><p>The military tradition starts in <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Gran Colombia</a>, where a sizable army was stationed in Ecuador due to border disputes with Peru, which claimed territories under its political control when it was a Spanish vice-royalty. Once Gran Colombia was dissolved after the death of <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Sim&#243;n Bol&#237;var">Sim&#243;n Bol&#237;var</a> in 1830, Ecuador inherited the same border disputes and had the need of creating its own professional military force. So influential was the military in Ecuador in the early republican period that its first decade was under the control of General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juan_Jose_Flores" title="Juan Jose Flores">Juan Jose Flores</a>, first president of Ecuador of Venezuelan origin. General Jose Ma. Urbina and General Robles are examples of military figures who became presidents of the country in the early republican period.\n</p><p>Due to the continuous border disputes with Peru, finally settled in the early 2000s, and due to the ongoing problem with the Colombian guerrilla insurgency infiltrating Amazonian provinces, the Ecuadorian Armed Forces has gone through a series of changes. In 2009, the new administration at the Defense Ministry launched a deep restructuring within the forces, increasing spending budget to $1,691,776,803, an increase of 25%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The icons of the Ecuadorian military forces are the Marshall Antonio Jos&#233; de Sucre and General <a href="/wiki/Eloy_Alfaro" title="Eloy Alfaro">Eloy Alfaro</a>. The Military Academy General Eloy Alfaro (c. 1838) graduates the army officers and is located in Quito.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The Ecuadorian Navy Academy (c. 1837), located in Salinas graduates the navy officers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> and the Air Academy "Cosme Rennella (c. 1920), also located in Salinas, graduates the air force officers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Other training academies for different military specialties are found across the country.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Ecuador" title="Geography of Ecuador">Geography of Ecuador</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_Topography.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1005" data-file-width="903" decoding="async" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ecuador_Topography.png/220px-Ecuador_Topography.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ecuador_Topography.png/330px-Ecuador_Topography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ecuador_Topography.png/440px-Ecuador_Topography.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_Topography.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ecuador topography</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Volc%C3%A1n_Cotopaxi_Ecuador.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1288" data-file-width="1936" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Volc%C3%A1n_Cotopaxi_Ecuador.JPG/170px-Volc%C3%A1n_Cotopaxi_Ecuador.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Volc%C3%A1n_Cotopaxi_Ecuador.JPG/255px-Volc%C3%A1n_Cotopaxi_Ecuador.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Volc%C3%A1n_Cotopaxi_Ecuador.JPG/340px-Volc%C3%A1n_Cotopaxi_Ecuador.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Volc%C3%A1n_Cotopaxi_Ecuador.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of the <a href="/wiki/Cotopaxi" title="Cotopaxi">Cotopaxi</a> volcano, in <a href="/wiki/Cotopaxi_Province" title="Cotopaxi Province">Cotopaxi Province</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Many_parrots_-Anangu,_Yasuni_National_Park,_Ecuador_-clay_lick-8.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3600" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Many_parrots_-Anangu%2C_Yasuni_National_Park%2C_Ecuador_-clay_lick-8.jpg/170px-Many_parrots_-Anangu%2C_Yasuni_National_Park%2C_Ecuador_-clay_lick-8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Many_parrots_-Anangu%2C_Yasuni_National_Park%2C_Ecuador_-clay_lick-8.jpg/255px-Many_parrots_-Anangu%2C_Yasuni_National_Park%2C_Ecuador_-clay_lick-8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Many_parrots_-Anangu%2C_Yasuni_National_Park%2C_Ecuador_-clay_lick-8.jpg/340px-Many_parrots_-Anangu%2C_Yasuni_National_Park%2C_Ecuador_-clay_lick-8.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Many_parrots_-Anangu,_Yasuni_National_Park,_Ecuador_-clay_lick-8.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>birds in the <a href="/wiki/Yasuni_National_Park" title="Yasuni National Park">Yasuni National Park</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Ecuador has a total area of 283,561&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (109,484&#160;sq&#160;mi), including the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Gal&#225;pagos Islands">Gal&#225;pagos Islands</a>. Of this, 276,841&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (106,889&#160;sq&#160;mi) is land and 6,720&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (2,595&#160;sq&#160;mi) water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAfactbook_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIAfactbook-5">[5]</a></sup> Ecuador is bigger than Uruguay, Suriname, Guyana and French Guyana in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>.\n</p><p>Ecuador lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/2nd_parallel_north" title="2nd parallel north">2&#176;N</a> and <a href="/wiki/5th_parallel_south" title="5th parallel south">5&#176;S</a>,\nbounded on the west by the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, and has 2,337&#160;km (1,452&#160;mi) of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coastline" title="Coastline">coastline</a>. It has 2,010&#160;km (1,250&#160;mi) of land boundaries, with <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> in the north 590&#160;km (367&#160;mi) border and Peru in the east and south 1,420&#160;km (882&#160;mi) border. It is the westernmost country that lies on the equator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The country has four main geographic regions:\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>La Costa</b>, or "the coast": The coastal region consists of the provinces to the West of the Andean range&#160;&#8211; <a href="/wiki/Esmeraldas_Province" title="Esmeraldas Province">Esmeraldas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guayas_Province" title="Guayas Province">Guayas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_R%C3%ADos_Province" title="Los R&#237;os Province">Los R&#237;os</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manab%C3%AD_Province" title="Manab&#237; Province">Manab&#237;</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Oro_Province" title="El Oro Province">El Oro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Elena_Province" title="Santa Elena Province">Santa Elena</a>. It is the country\'s most fertile and productive land, and is the seat of the large <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a> exportation plantations of the companies <a href="/wiki/Dole_Food_Company" title="Dole Food Company">Dole</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chiquita" title="Chiquita">Chiquita</a>. This region is also where most of Ecuador\'s <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> crop is grown. The truly coastal provinces have active fisheries. The largest coastal city is <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a>.</li>\n<li><b>La Sierra</b>, or "the highlands": The sierra consists of the Andean and Interandean highland provinces&#160;&#8211; <a href="/wiki/Azuay_Province" title="Azuay Province">Azuay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1ar_Province" title="Ca&#241;ar Province">Ca&#241;ar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carchi_Province" title="Carchi Province">Carchi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chimborazo_Province" title="Chimborazo Province">Chimborazo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imbabura_Province" title="Imbabura Province">Imbabura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loja_Province" title="Loja Province">Loja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pichincha_Province" title="Pichincha Province">Pichincha</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tungurahua_Province" title="Tungurahua Province">Tungurahua</a>. This land contains most of Ecuador\'s volcanoes and all of its snow-capped peaks. Agriculture is focused on the traditional crops of <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Quinoa" title="Quinoa">quinua</a> and the population is predominantly Amerindian <a href="/wiki/Quechua_people" title="Quechua people">Kichua</a>. The largest Sierran city is <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>.</li>\n<li><b>La Amazon&#237;a</b>, also known as <i>El Oriente</i>, or "the east": The oriente consists of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon jungle</a> provinces&#160;&#8211; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morona_Santiago_Province" title="Morona Santiago Province">Morona Santiago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Napo_Province" title="Napo Province">Napo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orellana_Province" title="Orellana Province">Orellana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pastaza_Province" title="Pastaza Province">Pastaza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sucumb%C3%ADos_Province" title="Sucumb&#237;os Province">Sucumb&#237;os</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zamora-Chinchipe_Province" title="Zamora-Chinchipe Province">Zamora-Chinchipe</a>. This region is primarily made up of the huge Amazon national parks and Amerindian untouchable zones, which are vast stretches of land set aside for the Amazon Amerindian tribes to continue living traditionally. It is also the area with the largest reserves of <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> in Ecuador, and parts of the upper Amazon here have been extensively exploited by petroleum companies. The population is primarily mixed Amerindian <a href="/wiki/Shuar" title="Shuar">Shuar</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huaorani" title="Huaorani">Huaorani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quechua_people" title="Quechua people">Kichua</a>, although there are numerous tribes in the deep jungle which are little-contacted. The largest city in the Oriente is probably <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Loja" title="Nueva Loja">Lago Agrio</a> in Sucumb&#237;os, although <a href="/wiki/Macas_(city)" title="Macas (city)">Macas</a> in Morona Santiago runs a close second.</li>\n<li><b>La Regi&#243;n Insular</b> is the region comprising the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Gal&#225;pagos Islands">Gal&#225;pagos Islands</a>, some 1,000 kilometres (620&#160;mi) west of the mainland in the Pacific Ocean.</li></ul>\n<p>Ecuador\'s capital is Quito, which is in the province of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pichincha_Province,_Ecuador" title="Pichincha Province, Ecuador">Pichincha</a> in the Sierra region. Its largest city is Guayaquil, in the <a href="/wiki/Guayas_Province" title="Guayas Province">Guayas Province</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cotopaxi" title="Cotopaxi">Cotopaxi</a>, just south of Quito, is one of the world\'s highest active volcanoes. The top of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chimborazo_(volcano)" title="Chimborazo (volcano)">Mount Chimborazo</a> (6,268 m, or 20,560&#160;ft, above sea level), Ecuador\'s tallest mountain, is the most distant point from the center of the Earth on the Earth\'s surface because of the <a href="/wiki/Ellipsoid" title="Ellipsoid">ellipsoid</a> shape of the planet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Ecuador" title="Climate of Ecuador">Climate of Ecuador</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1465" data-file-width="1900" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ecuador map of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen climate classification</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>There is great variety in the climate, largely determined by altitude. It is mild year-round in the mountain valleys, with a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> in coastal areas and <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a> in lowlands. The Pacific coastal area has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a> with a severe rainy season. The climate in the Andean highlands is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperateness" title="Temperateness">temperate</a> and relatively dry, and the Amazon basin on the eastern side of the mountains shares the climate of other rainforest zones.\n</p><p>Because of its location at the equator, Ecuador experiences little variation in daylight hours during the course of a year. Both sunrise and sunset occur each day at the two six o\'clock hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrology">Hydrology</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rivers_of_Ecuador" title="Rivers of Ecuador">Rivers of Ecuador</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="648" data-file-width="486" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG/170px-Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG/255px-Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG/340px-Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa" title="Ba&#241;os de Agua Santa">Ba&#241;os de Agua Santa</a> is an important tourist site</div></div></div>\n<p>The Andes is the <i>watershed divisor</i> between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" title="Amazon Basin">Amazon</a> watershed, which runs to the east, and the Pacific, including the north&#8211;south rivers Mataje, Santiago, <a href="/wiki/Esmeraldas_River" title="Esmeraldas River">Esmeraldas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chone_River" title="Chone River">Chone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guayas_River" title="Guayas River">Guayas</a>, Jubones, and Puyango-Tumbes.\n</p><p>Almost all of the rivers in Ecuador form in the La Sierra region and flow east toward the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon River</a> or west toward the Pacific Ocean. The rivers rise from snowmelt at the edges of the snowcapped peaks or from the abundant precipitation that falls at higher elevations. In the La Sierra region, the streams and rivers are narrow and flow rapidly over precipitous slopes. Rivers may slow and widen as they cross the hoyas yet become rapid again as they flow from the heights of the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> to the lower elevations of the other regions. The highland rivers broaden as they enter the more level areas of the Costa and the Oriente.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg/220px-Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg/330px-Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg/440px-Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A beach of <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Ecuador" title="Salinas, Ecuador">Salinas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Elena_Province" title="Santa Elena Province">Santa Elena Province</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In the Costa, the external coast has mostly intermittent rivers that are fed by constant rains from December through May and become empty riverbeds during the dry season. The few exceptions are the longer, perennial rivers that flow throughout the external coast from the internal coast and La Sierra on their way to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. The internal coast, by contrast, is crossed by perennial rivers that may flood during the rainy season, sometimes forming swamps.\n</p><p>Major rivers in the Oriente include the <a href="/wiki/Pastaza_River" title="Pastaza River">Pastaza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Napo_River" title="Napo River">Napo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Putumayo_River" title="Putumayo River">Putumayo</a>. The Pastaza is formed by the confluence of the Chambo and the Patate rivers, both of which rise in the Sierra. The Pastaza includes the Agoyan waterfall, which at sixty-one meters (200 feet) is the highest waterfall in Ecuador. The Napo rises near Mount Cotopaxi and is the major river used for transport in the eastern lowlands. The Napo ranges in width from 500 to 1,800&#160;m (1,600 to 5,900&#160;ft). In its upper reaches, the Napo flows rapidly until the confluence with one of its major tributaries, the Coca River, where it slows and levels off. The Putumayo forms part of the border with Colombia. All of these rivers flow into the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon River</a>. The Gal&#225;pagos Islands have no significant rivers. Several of the larger islands, however, have freshwater springs although they are surrounded by the Pacific Ocean.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_-_Serran%C3%ADas_Cof%C3%A1n-Bermejo,_Sinangoe_(2002)_(21157752225).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3655" data-file-width="2673" decoding="async" height="273" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Ecuador_-_Serran%C3%ADas_Cof%C3%A1n-Bermejo%2C_Sinangoe_%282002%29_%2821157752225%29.jpg/200px-Ecuador_-_Serran%C3%ADas_Cof%C3%A1n-Bermejo%2C_Sinangoe_%282002%29_%2821157752225%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Ecuador_-_Serran%C3%ADas_Cof%C3%A1n-Bermejo%2C_Sinangoe_%282002%29_%2821157752225%29.jpg/300px-Ecuador_-_Serran%C3%ADas_Cof%C3%A1n-Bermejo%2C_Sinangoe_%282002%29_%2821157752225%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Ecuador_-_Serran%C3%ADas_Cof%C3%A1n-Bermejo%2C_Sinangoe_%282002%29_%2821157752225%29.jpg/400px-Ecuador_-_Serran%C3%ADas_Cof%C3%A1n-Bermejo%2C_Sinangoe_%282002%29_%2821157752225%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_-_Serran%C3%ADas_Cof%C3%A1n-Bermejo,_Sinangoe_(2002)_(21157752225).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ecuador is one of the most <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse countries</a> in the world, it also has the most biodiversity per square kilometer of any nation, and is one of the highest <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemism</a> worldwide. In the image the <a href="/wiki/Spectacled_bear" title="Spectacled bear">Spectacled bear</a> of the Andes.</div></div></div>\n<p>Ecuador is one of seventeen <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse countries</a> in the world according to Conservation International,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conservation_International_Site_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Conservation_International_Site-12">[12]</a></sup> and it has the most biodiversity per square kilometer of any nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ecuador has 1,600 bird species (15% of the world\'s known bird species) in the continental area and 38 more <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> in the Gal&#225;pagos. In addition to over 16,000 species of plants, the country has 106 endemic reptiles, 138 endemic amphibians, and 6,000 species of butterfly. The Gal&#225;pagos Islands are well known as a region of distinct fauna, famous as the place of birth of Darwin\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theory_of_Evolution" title="Theory of Evolution">Theory of Evolution</a> and a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> World Heritage Site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ecuador has the first constitution to recognize the rights of nature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The protection of the nation\'s biodiversity is an explicit national priority as stated in the National Plan of "Buen Vivir", or good living, Objective 4, "Guarantee the rights of nature", Policy 1: "Sustainably conserve and manage the natural heritage, including its land and marine biodiversity, which is considered a strategic sector".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> As of the writing of the Plan in 2008, 19% of Ecuador\'s land area was in a protected area; however, the Plan also states that 32% of the land must be protected in order to truly preserve the nation\'s biodiversity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir-40">[40]</a></sup> Current <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_in_Ecuador" title="List of national parks in Ecuador">protected areas</a> include 11 national parks, 10 wildlife refuges, 9 ecological reserves, and other areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> A program begun in 2008, Sociobosque, is preserving another 2.3% of total land area (6,295&#160;km&#178;, or 629,500 ha) by paying private landowners or community landowners (such as Amerindian tribes) incentives to maintain their land as native ecosystems such as native forests or grasslands. Eligibility and subsidy rates for this program are determined based on the poverty in the region, the number of hectares that will be protected, and the type of ecosystem of the land to be protected, among other factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite being on the UNESCO list, the Gal&#225;pagos are endangered by a range of negative environmental effects, threatening the existence of this exotic <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystem</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Additionally, oil exploitation of the Amazon rainforest has led to the release of billions of gallons of untreated wastes, gas, and crude oil into the environment, contaminating ecosystems and causing detrimental health effects to Amerindian peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Ecuador" title="Economy of Ecuador">Economy of Ecuador</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="954" data-file-width="932" decoding="async" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png/220px-Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png/330px-Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png/440px-Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tree map of products exported by Ecuador in the HS4 product classification.</div></div></div>\n<p>Ecuador has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_economy" title="Developing economy">developing economy</a> that is highly dependent on commodities, namely petroleum and agricultural products. The country is classified as an upper-middle-income country. Ecuador\'s economy is the eighth largest in Latin America and experienced an average growth of 4.6% between 2000 and 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> From 2007 to 2012 Ecuador\'s GDP grew at an annual average of 4.3 percent, above the average for Latin America and the Caribbean, which was 3.5%, according to the United Nations\' Economic Commission for Latin American and the Caribbean (ECLAC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Ecuador was able to maintain relatively superior growth during the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007&#8211;2008">crisis</a>. In January 2009 the Central Bank of Ecuador (BCE) put the 2010 growth forecast at 6.88%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In 2011 its GDP grew at 8% and ranked 3rd highest in Latin America, behind Argentina (2nd) and Panama (1st).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Between 1999 and 2007, GDP doubled, reaching $65,490 million according to BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>\nInflation rate up to January 2008 was located about 1.14%, the highest recorded in the last year, according to the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The monthly unemployment rate remained at about 6 and 8 percent from December 2007 until September 2008; however, it went up to about 9 percent in October and dropped again in November 2008 to 8 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Unemployment mean annual rate for 2009 in Ecuador was 8.5% because the global economic crisis continued to affect the Latin American economies. From this point unemployment rates started a downward trend: 7.6% in 2010, 6.0% in 2011, and 4.8% in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The extreme poverty rate has declined significantly between 1999 and 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> In 2001 it was estimated at 40% of the population, while by 2011 the figure dropped to 17.4% of the total population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economy_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-economy-59">[59]</a></sup> This is explained to an extent by emigration and the economic stability achieved after adopting the U.S. dollar as official means of transaction (prior to 2000 the Ecuadorian <i><a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_sucre" title="Ecuadorian sucre">sucre</a></i> was prone to rampant inflation). However, starting in 2008 with the bad economic performance of the nations where most Ecuadorian emigrants work, the reduction of poverty has been realized through social spending mainly in education and health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Obverse_of_the_series_2009_$100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="505" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Obverse_of_the_series_2009_%24100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg/250px-Obverse_of_the_series_2009_%24100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Obverse_of_the_series_2009_%24100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg/375px-Obverse_of_the_series_2009_%24100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Obverse_of_the_series_2009_%24100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg/500px-Obverse_of_the_series_2009_%24100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Obverse_of_the_series_2009_$100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a> is the common currency circulation in Ecuador.</div></div></div>\n<p>Oil accounts for 40% of exports and contributes to maintaining a positive trade balance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Since the late 1960s, the exploitation of oil increased production, and proven reserves are estimated at 6.51 billion barrels as of  2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The overall trade balance for August 2012 was a surplus of almost $390 million for the first six months of 2012, a huge figure compared with that of 2007, which reached only $5.7 million; the surplus had risen by about $425 million compared to 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economy_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-economy-59">[59]</a></sup> The oil trade balance positive had revenues of $3.295 million in 2008, while non-oil was negative, amounting to $2.842 million. The trade balance with the United States, Chile, the European Union, Bolivia, Peru, Brazil, and Mexico is positive. The trade balance with Argentina, Colombia, and Asia is negative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the agricultural sector, Ecuador is a major exporter of bananas (first place worldwide in production and export), flowers, and the seventh largest producer of cocoa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Ecuador also produces coffee, rice, potatoes, cassava (manioc, tapioca), plantains and sugarcane; cattle, sheep, pigs, beef, pork and dairy products; fish, and shrimp; and balsa wood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The country\'s vast resources include large amounts of timber across the country, like eucalyptus and mangroves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Resources_Maps_World_Banks_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Resources_Maps_World_Banks-66">[66]</a></sup> Pines and cedars are planted in the region of La Sierra and walnuts, rosemary, and balsa wood in the Guayas River Basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup>\nThe industry is concentrated mainly in Guayaquil, the largest industrial center, and in Quito, where in recent years the industry has grown considerably. This city is also the largest business center of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Industrial production is directed primarily to the domestic market.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Despite this, there is limited export of products produced or processed industrially.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> These include canned foods, liquor, jewelry, furniture, and more.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A minor industrial activity is also concentrated in Cuenca.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Industrias_en_Cuenca_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Industrias_en_Cuenca-69">[69]</a></sup> The incomes due to the tourism have been increasing during the last years because of the efforts of the Government of showing the variety of climates and the biodiversity in Ecuador.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wtcgye.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="2892" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Wtcgye.jpg/180px-Wtcgye.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Wtcgye.jpg/270px-Wtcgye.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Wtcgye.jpg/360px-Wtcgye.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wtcgye.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>World Trade Center headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Ecuador has negotiated bilateral treaties with other countries, besides belonging to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andean_Community_of_Nations" title="Andean Community of Nations">Andean Community of Nations</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> and an associate member of <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> It also serves on the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO), in addition to the <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Development_Bank" title="Inter-American Development Bank">Inter-American Development Bank</a> (IDB), <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corporaci%C3%B3n_Andina_de_Fomento" title="Corporaci&#243;n Andina de Fomento">Corporaci&#243;n Andina de Fomento</a> (CAF) and other multilateral agencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> In April 2007, Ecuador paid off its debt to the IMF, thus ending an era of interventionism of the Agency in the country.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\nThe public finance of Ecuador consists of the Central Bank of Ecuador (BCE), the National Development Bank (BNF), the State Bank.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Ecuador" title="Tourism in Ecuador">Tourism in Ecuador</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roof_deck_(Palacio_de_Pizarro),_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_(Quito),_pic.aa4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3672" data-file-width="4896" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Roof_deck_%28Palacio_de_Pizarro%29%2C_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_%28Quito%29%2C_pic.aa4.jpg/220px-Roof_deck_%28Palacio_de_Pizarro%29%2C_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_%28Quito%29%2C_pic.aa4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Roof_deck_%28Palacio_de_Pizarro%29%2C_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_%28Quito%29%2C_pic.aa4.jpg/330px-Roof_deck_%28Palacio_de_Pizarro%29%2C_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_%28Quito%29%2C_pic.aa4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Roof_deck_%28Palacio_de_Pizarro%29%2C_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_%28Quito%29%2C_pic.aa4.jpg/440px-Roof_deck_%28Palacio_de_Pizarro%29%2C_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_%28Quito%29%2C_pic.aa4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roof_deck_(Palacio_de_Pizarro),_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_(Quito),_pic.aa4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The historic center of <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a> has one of the largest and best-preserved historic centers in the Americas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The city also houses a large number of museums.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Ministry of Information and Tourism was created on August 10, 1992, at the beginning of the government of <a href="/wiki/Sixto_Dur%C3%A1n_Ball%C3%A9n" title="Sixto Dur&#225;n Ball&#233;n">Sixto Dur&#225;n Ball&#233;n</a>, who viewed tourism as a fundamental activity for the economic and social development of the peoples. Faced with the growth of the tourism sector, in June 1994, the decision was taken to separate tourism from information, so that it is exclusively dedicated to promoting and strengthening this activity.\n</p><p>Ecuador is a country with vast natural wealth. The diversity of its four regions has given rise to thousands of species of flora and fauna. It has around 1640 kinds of birds. The species of butterflies border the 4,500, the reptiles 345, the amphibians 358 and the mammals 258, among others. Not in vain, Ecuador is considered one of the 17 countries where the planet\'s highest biodiversity is concentrated, being also the largest country with diversity per km2 in the world. Most of its fauna and flora lives in 26 protected areas by the State. Also, it has a huge culture spectrum. Since 2007, with the government of Rafael Correa, the tourism brand "Ecuador Ama la Vida" has been transformed, with which the nation\'s tourism promotion would be sold. Focused on considering it as a country friendly and respectful of the nature, natural biodiversity and cultural diversity of the peoples. And for this, means of exploiting them are developed along with the private economy.\n</p><p>The country has two cities UNESCO World Heritage Sites: Quito and Cuenca, as well as two natural UNESCO World Heritage Sites: the Galapagos Islands and Sangay National Park in addition to one <a href="/wiki/World_Network_of_Biosphere_Reserves" title="World Network of Biosphere Reserves">World Biosphere Reserve</a>, such as the Cajas massif. Culturally, the Toquilla straw hat and the culture of the Zapara indigenous people are recognized. The most popular sites for national and foreign tourists have different nuances due to the various tourist activities offered by the country.\n</p><p>Among the main tourist destinations are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Nature attractions: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galapagos_Islands" title="Galapagos Islands">Galapagos Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yasuni_National_Park" title="Yasuni National Park">Yasuni National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Cajas_National_Park" title="El Cajas National Park">El Cajas National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sangay_National_Park" title="Sangay National Park">Sangay National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Podocarpus_National_Park" title="Podocarpus National Park">Podocarpus National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vilcabamba,_Ecuador" title="Vilcabamba, Ecuador">Vilcabamba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa" title="Ba&#241;os de Agua Santa">Ba&#241;os de Agua Santa</a>.</li></ul>\n<ul><li>Cultural attractions: <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Historic center of Quito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Mitad_del_Mundo" title="Ciudad Mitad del Mundo">Ciudad Mitad del Mundo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ingapirca" title="Ingapirca">Ingapirca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuenca,_Ecuador" title="Cuenca, Ecuador">Historic center of Cuenca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latacunga" title="Latacunga">Latacunga</a> and its Mama Negra festival.</li></ul>\n<ul><li>Snowy mountains: <a href="/wiki/Antisana" title="Antisana">Antisana</a> volcano, <a href="/wiki/Cayambe_(volcano)" title="Cayambe (volcano)">Cayambe</a> volcano, <a href="/wiki/Chimborazo" title="Chimborazo">Chimborazo</a> volcano, <a href="/wiki/Cotopaxi" title="Cotopaxi">Cotopaxi</a> volcano, <a href="/wiki/Illiniza" title="Illiniza">Illinizas</a> volcanoes.</li></ul>\n<ul><li>Beaches: Crucita, <a href="/wiki/Atacames" title="Atacames">Atacames</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%ADa_de_Car%C3%A1quez" title="Bah&#237;a de Car&#225;quez">Bah&#237;a de Car&#225;quez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esmeraldas,_Ecuador" title="Esmeraldas, Ecuador">Esmeraldas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manta,_Ecuador" title="Manta, Ecuador">Manta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Ecuador" title="Salinas, Ecuador">Salinas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monta%C3%B1ita" title="Monta&#241;ita">Monta&#241;ita</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1738" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg/220px-Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg/330px-Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg/440px-Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Quito" title="Trolleybuses in Quito">Troleb&#250;s</a> bus rapid transit system that runs through <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>. It is the principal BRT in Ecuador.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Railways_in_Ecuador.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="588" decoding="async" height="299" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Railways_in_Ecuador.svg/220px-Railways_in_Ecuador.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Railways_in_Ecuador.svg/330px-Railways_in_Ecuador.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Railways_in_Ecuador.svg/440px-Railways_in_Ecuador.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Railways_in_Ecuador.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Railways in Ecuador <span class="nowrap">(<a class="extiw" href="//sharemap.org/public/Railways_in_Ecuador" title="sharemap:public/Railways in Ecuador">interactive map</a>)</span></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Ecuador" title="Transport in Ecuador">Transport in Ecuador</a></div>\n<p>The rehabilitation and reopening of the Ecuadorian railroad and use of it as a tourist attraction is one of the recent developments in transportation matters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The roads of Ecuador in recent years have undergone important improvement. The major routes are Pan American (under enhancement from four to six lanes from Rumichaca to Ambato, the conclusion of 4 lanes on the entire stretch of Ambato and Riobamba and running via Riobamba to Loja). In the absence of the section between Loja and the border with Peru, there are the Route Espondilus and/or Ruta del Sol (oriented to travel along the Ecuadorian coastline) and the Amazon backbone (which crosses from north to south along the Ecuadorian Amazon, linking most and more major cities of it).\n</p><p>Another major project is developing the road Manta &#8211; Tena, the highway Guayaquil &#8211; Salinas Highway Aloag Santo Domingo, Riobamba &#8211; Macas (which crosses Sangay National Park). Other new developments include the National Unity bridge complex in Guayaquil, the bridge over the Napo river in Francisco de Orellana, the Esmeraldas River Bridge in the city of the same name, and, perhaps the most remarkable of all, the Bahia &#8211; San Vincente Bridge, being the largest on the Latin American Pacific coast.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mariscal_Sucre_International_Airport" title="Mariscal Sucre International Airport">Mariscal Sucre International Airport</a> in Quito and the <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Joaqu%C3%ADn_de_Olmedo_International_Airport" title="Jos&#233; Joaqu&#237;n de Olmedo International Airport">Jos&#233; Joaqu&#237;n de Olmedo International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a> have experienced a high increase in demand and have required modernization. In the case of Guayaquil it involved a new air terminal, once considered the best in South America and the best in Latin America<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> and in Quito where an entire new airport has been built in Tababela and was inaugurated in February 2013, with Canadian assistance. However, the main road leading from Quito city centre to the new airport will only be finished in late 2014, making current travelling from the airport to downtown Quito as long as two hours during rush hour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Quito\'s old city-centre airport is being turned into parkland, with some light industrial use.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_people" title="Ecuadorian people">Ecuadorian people</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ecuador_2016.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="610" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ecuador_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ecuador_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ecuador_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ecuador_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ecuador_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ecuador_2016.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Ecuador_2016.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population pyramid 2016</div></div></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i>Three mulattomen from Esmeraldas</i> by Andr&#233;s S&#225;nchez Galque. Painting of 1599. <a href="/wiki/Quito_School" title="Quito School">Quito Painting Colonial School</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Retrato_de_una_se%C3%B1ora_principal_con_su_negra_esclava_por_Vicente_Alb%C3%A1n.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1214" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Retrato_de_una_se%C3%B1ora_principal_con_su_negra_esclava_por_Vicente_Alb%C3%A1n.jpg/200px-Retrato_de_una_se%C3%B1ora_principal_con_su_negra_esclava_por_Vicente_Alb%C3%A1n.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Retrato_de_una_se%C3%B1ora_principal_con_su_negra_esclava_por_Vicente_Alb%C3%A1n.jpg/300px-Retrato_de_una_se%C3%B1ora_principal_con_su_negra_esclava_por_Vicente_Alb%C3%A1n.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Retrato_de_una_se%C3%B1ora_principal_con_su_negra_esclava_por_Vicente_Alb%C3%A1n.jpg/400px-Retrato_de_una_se%C3%B1ora_principal_con_su_negra_esclava_por_Vicente_Alb%C3%A1n.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i>Portrait of a noble lady with her black slave</i> by Vicente Alb&#225;n. Painting of 1783. <a href="/wiki/Quito_School" title="Quito School">Quito Painting Colonial School</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Ecuador\'s population is ethnically diverse and the 2016 estimates put Ecuador\'s population at 16,385,068.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-6">[6]</a></sup> The largest ethnic group (as of  2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>) is the <i><a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">Mestizos</a></i>, who are the descendants of Spanish colonists that interbred with Amerindian peoples, and constitute about 71% of the population. The White Ecuadorians (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Latin_American" title="White Latin American">White Latin American</a>) account for 6.1% of the population of Ecuador and can be found throughout all of Ecuador primarily around the urban areas. Even though Ecuador\'s white population during its colonial era were mainly descendants from Spain, today Ecuador\'s white population is a result of a mixture of European immigrants, predominantly from Spain with people from Italy, France, Germany, and Switzerland who have settled in the early 20th century. Ecuador also has people of middle eastern extraction that have also joined the ranks of the white minority. These include economically well off immigrants of Lebanese and Palestinian descent, who are either Christian or Muslim (<a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Ecuador" title="Islam in Ecuador">Islam in Ecuador</a>). In addition, there is a small European Jewish (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Jews" title="Ecuadorian Jews">Ecuadorian Jews</a>) population, which is based mainly in Quito and to a lesser extent in Guayaquil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethn_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-ethn-3">[3]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_Peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous Peoples of the Americas">Amerindians</a> account for 7% of the current population. The mostly rural Montubio population of the coastal provinces of Ecuador, who might be classified as <a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">Pardo</a> account for 7.4% of the population. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Ecuadorian_people" title="Afro-Ecuadorian people">Afro-Ecuadorians</a> is a minority population (7%) in Ecuador, that includes the <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">Mulattos</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Zambo" title="Zambo">zambos</a></i>, and are largely based in the Esmeraldas province and to a lesser degree in the predominantly Mestizo provinces of Coastal Ecuador - Guayas and Manabi. In the Highland Andes where a predominantly Mestizo, white and Amerindian population exist, the African presence is almost non-existent except for a small community in the province of Imbabura called Chota Valley.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Ecuador" title="Religion in Ecuador">Religion in Ecuador</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_en_la_ciudad_de_Cuenca,_Ecuador.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Iglesia_de_San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_en_la_ciudad_de_Cuenca%2C_Ecuador.JPG/220px-Iglesia_de_San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_en_la_ciudad_de_Cuenca%2C_Ecuador.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Iglesia_de_San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_en_la_ciudad_de_Cuenca%2C_Ecuador.JPG/330px-Iglesia_de_San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_en_la_ciudad_de_Cuenca%2C_Ecuador.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Iglesia_de_San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_en_la_ciudad_de_Cuenca%2C_Ecuador.JPG/440px-Iglesia_de_San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_en_la_ciudad_de_Cuenca%2C_Ecuador.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_en_la_ciudad_de_Cuenca,_Ecuador.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Iglesia de San Sebasti&#225;n church in <a href="/wiki/Cuenca,_Ecuador" title="Cuenca, Ecuador">Cuenca</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Ecuadorians" title="Black Ecuadorians">Black</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:pink; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:gold; width:0.4%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.4%</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>According to the Ecuadorian National Institute of Statistics and Census, 91.95% of the country\'s population have a religion, 7.94% are <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheists</a> and 0.11% are <a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">agnostics</a>. Among the people that have a religion, 80.44% are Roman Catholic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_Rite" title="Latin Rite">Latin Rite</a> (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Roman_Catholic_dioceses_in_Ecuador" title="List of Roman Catholic dioceses in Ecuador">List of Roman Catholic dioceses in Ecuador</a>), 11.30% are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical" title="Evangelical">Evangelical</a> <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a>, 1.29% are <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah\'s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a> and 6.97% other (mainly Jewish, Buddhists and Latter-day Saints).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_San_Francisco,_Quito_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3055" data-file-width="4583" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Iglesia_de_San_Francisco%2C_Quito_01.jpg/220px-Iglesia_de_San_Francisco%2C_Quito_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Iglesia_de_San_Francisco%2C_Quito_01.jpg/330px-Iglesia_de_San_Francisco%2C_Quito_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Iglesia_de_San_Francisco%2C_Quito_01.jpg/440px-Iglesia_de_San_Francisco%2C_Quito_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_San_Francisco,_Quito_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Iglesia_y_Convento_de_San_Francisco,_Quito" title="Iglesia y Convento de San Francisco, Quito">Iglesia y Convento de San Francisco</a> in <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In the rural parts of Ecuador, Amerindian beliefs and Catholicism are sometimes <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretized</a>. Most festivals and annual parades are based on religious celebrations, many incorporating a mixture of rites and icons.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>There is a small number of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Christians</a>, Amerindian religions, Muslims (see <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Ecuador" title="Islam in Ecuador">Islam in Ecuador</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhists</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD" title="Bah&#225;\'&#237;">Bah&#225;\'&#237;</a>. According to their own estimates, <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> accounts for about 1.4% of the population, or 211,165 members at the end of 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> According to their own sources, in 2017 there were 92,752 <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah\'s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a> in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first Jews arrived in Ecuador in the 16th and 17th centuries. Most of them are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sephardic" title="Sephardic">Sephardic</a> <a href="/wiki/Anusim" title="Anusim">Anusim</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crypto-Jews" title="Crypto-Jews">Crypto-Jews</a>) and many still speak <a href="/wiki/Judaeo-Spanish" title="Judaeo-Spanish">Judaeo-Spanish</a> (Ladino) language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Today the Jewish Community of Ecuador (Comunidad Jud&#237;a del Ecuador) has its seat in <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a> and has approximately 200 members. Nevertheless, this number is declining because young people leave the country for the United States or <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. The Community has a Jewish Center with a <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogue</a>, a country club, and a cemetery. It supports the "Albert Einstein School", where Jewish history, religion, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hebrew" title="Hebrew">Hebrew</a> classes are offered.\nThere are very small communities in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuenca_(Ecuador)" title="Cuenca (Ecuador)">Cuenca</a>. The "Comunidad de Culto Israelita" reunites the Jews of <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a>. This community works independently from the "Jewish Community of Ecuador" and is composed of only 30 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nations">Nations</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Ecuador" title="Indigenous peoples in Ecuador">Indigenous peoples in Ecuador</a></div>\n<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ddd"><th colspan="5" style="text-align:center;">Ethnic groups in Ecuador<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAPAPUANEWGUINEA_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIAPAPUANEWGUINEA-79">[79]</a></sup></th></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:88%; text-align: right;">4.3%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mulato" title="Mulato">Mulato</a> </td>\n<td style="width: 100px;
